em	A										<p>This unit represents the calculated font-size of the element. If used on the font-size property itself, it represents the inherited font-size of the element. This unit is often used to create scalable layouts, which keep the vertical rhythm of the page, even when the user changes the size of the fonts. The CSS properties line-height, font-size, margin-bottom and margin-top often have values expressed in em.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#em
ex	A										<p>This unit represents the x-height of the element's font. On fonts with the 'x' letter, this is generally the height of lowercase letters in the font; 1ex ≈ 0.5em in many fonts.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#ex
ch	A										<p>This unit represents the width, or more precisely the advance measure, of the glyph '0' (zero, the Unicode character U+0030) in the element's font.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#ch
rem	A										<p>This unit represents the font-size of the root element (e.g. the font-size of the <html> element). When used on the font-size on this root element, it represents its initial value. This unit is practical in creating perfectly scalable layout. If not supported by the targeted browsers, such layout can be achieved using the em unit, though this is slightly more complex.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#rem
vh	A										<p>1/100th of the height of the viewport.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#vh
vw	A										<p>1/100th of the width of the viewport.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#vw
vmin	A										<p>1/100th of the minimum value between the height and the width of the viewport.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#vmin
vmax	A										<p>1/100th of the maximum value between the height and the width of the viewport.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#vmax
px	A										<p>Relative to the viewing device. For screen display, typically one device pixel (dot) of the display. For printers and very high resolution screens one CSS pixel implies multiple device pixels, so that the number of pixel per inch stays around 96.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#px
mm	A										<p>One millimeter.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#mm
q	A										<p>A quarter of a millimeter (1/40th of a centimeter).</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#q
cm	A										<p>One centimeter (10 millimeters).</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#cm
in	A										<p>One inch (2.54 centimeters).</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#in
pt	A										<p>One point (1/72th of an inch).</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#pt
pc	A										<p>One pica (12 points).</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#pc
mozmm	A										<p>An experimental unit which attempts to render at exactly one millimeter regardless of the size or resolution of the display. This is rarely actually what you want, but may be useful in particular for mobile devices.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length#mozmm

It is a number immediately followed by a length unit (px, em, pc, in, mm, …). Like for any CSS dimension, there is no space between the unit literal and the number. The length unit is optional after the number 0.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/length

It can't be in %. */\nrepeating-radial-gradient( ellipse x-axis y-axis, … ) /* The two semi-major axis are given, horizontal, then vertical */\n\nDefinition of the position of the shape\nrepeating-radial-gradient (… at <position>, … )\n\nDefinition of the color stops\nrepeating-radial-gradient (…, <color-stop>)\nrepeating-radial-gradient (…, <color-stop>, <color-stop>)</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-radial-gradient

Media queries, added in CSS3, let the presentation of content be tailored to a specific range of output devices without having to change the content itself.</p><br><pre><code><!-- CSS media query on a link element -->\n<link rel="stylesheet" media="(max-width: 800px)" href="example.css" />\n\n<!-- CSS media query within a stylesheet -->\n<style>\n@media (max-width: 600px) {\n .facet_sidebar {\n display: none;\n }\n}\n</style></code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Media_Queries/Using_media_queries

This style may be overridden by any other link-related pseudo-classes, that is :link, :visited, and :active, appearing in subsequent rules. In order to style appropriately links, you need to put the :hover rule after the :link and :visited rules but before the :active one, as defined by the LVHA-order : :link — :visited — :hover — :active.</p><br><pre><code>:hover { style properties }</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/:hover

Just as is the case with all other units in CSS, there isn't a space between the '%' and the number.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/percentage

gradient	A										<p>The gradient CSS data type denotes a CSS image made of a progressive transition between two or more colors. A CSS gradient is not a CSS color but an image with no intrinsic dimensions ; that is, it has no natural or preferred size, nor a preferred ratio. Its concrete size will match the one of the element it applies to.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/gradient

Like these two other CSS-wide keywords, it can be applied to any CSS property, including the CSS shorthand all. This keyword resets the property to its inherited value if it inherits from its parent or to its initial value if not. In other words, it behaves like the inherit keyword in the first case and like the initial keyword in the second case.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/unset

Values are separated by a comma to indicate that they are alternatives. The result of this function is an object of the CSS gradient data type. Like any other gradient, a CSS linear gradient is not a CSS color but an image with no intrinsic dimensions ; that is, it has neither natural or preferred size, nor ratio. Its concrete size will match the size of the element it applies to.</p><br><pre><code>linear-gradient( 45deg, blue, red ); /* A gradient on 45deg axis starting blue and finishing red */\nlinear-gradient( to left top, blue, red); /* A gradient going from the bottom right to the top left starting blue and \n finishing red */\n\nlinear-gradient( 0deg, blue, green 40%, red ); /* A gradient going from the bottom to top, starting blue, being green after 40% \n and finishing red */</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/linear-gradient

The clipping region is a path specified as a URL referencing an inline or external SVG, or shape method such as circle(). The clip-path property replaces the now deprecated clip property.</p><br><pre><code>/* Keyword values */\nclip-path: none;\nclip-path: fill-box;\nclip-path: stroke-box;\nclip-path: view-box;\n\n/* Image values */\nclip-path: url(resources.svg#c1);\n\n/* Geometry values */\nclip-path: inset(100px 50px);\nclip-path: circle(50px at 0 100px);\nclip-path: polygon(50% 0%, 100% 50%, 50% 100%, 0% 50%);\n\n/* Global values */\nclip-path: inherit;\nclip-path: initial;\nclip-path: unset;</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/clip-path

Any other scrolls, e.g. those that are performed by the user, are not affected by this property. replaced element	A							[Summary https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Replaced_element#Summary]\\n[See also https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Replaced_element#See_also]\\n			<p>In CSS, a replaced element is an element whose representation is outside the scope of CSS. These are a type of external object whose representation is independent of the CSS. Typical replaced elements are img, object, video or form elements like textarea and input. Some elements, like audio or canvas are replaced elements only in specific cases. Objects inserted using the CSS content properties are anonymous replaced elements.</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/Replaced_element

The column-width is the maximum width a column will become before adding another column. For instance, a 300px column width a gap of 0px would be a single column at 599px, but at 600px it would be split into 2 columns. This allows us to achieve scalable designs that fit different screen sizes. Especially in presence of the column-count CSS property which has precedence, to set an exact column width, all length values must be specified. In horizontal text these are width, column-width, column-gap, and column-rule-width.</p><br><pre><code>/* Keyword value */\ncolumn-width: auto;\n\n/* Different <length> values */\ncolumn-width: 6px;\ncolumn-width: 25em;\ncolumn-width: 0.3vw;\n\n/* Global values */\ncolumn-width: inherit;\ncolumn-width: initial;\ncolumn-width: unset;</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/column-width

repeating-linear-gradient()	A							[Syntax https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient#Syntax]\\n[Values https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient#Values]\\n[Formal syntax https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient#Formal_syntax]\\n[Examples https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient#Examples]\\n[Specifications https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient#Specifications]\\n[Browser compatibility https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient#Browser_compatibility]\\n[See also https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient#See_also]\\n			<p>The CSS repeating-linear-gradient function creates an image consisting of repeating gradients. It works similarly to the basic linear gradients as described by linear-gradient(), and takes the same arguments. However, it automatically repeats the color stops infinitely in both directions. The color stops' positions shift by multiples of the length of a basic linear gradient (the difference between the last color stops' position and the first).</p><br><pre><code>repeating-linear-gradient(45deg, blue, red); /* A repeating gradient on 45deg axe starting blue and finishing red */\nrepeating-linear-gradient(to left top, blue, red); /* A repeating gradient going from the bottom right to the top left \n starting blue and finishing red */\n\nrepeating-linear-gradient(0deg, blue, green 40%, red); /* A repeating gradient going from the bottom to top, starting blue, \n being green after 40% and finishing red */</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/repeating-linear-gradient

revert	A							[Example https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/revert#Example]\\n[Specifications https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/revert#Specifications]\\n[Browser compatibility https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/revert#Browser_compatibility]\\n[See also https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/revert#See_also]\\n			<p>The revert CSS keyword rolls back the cascade so that the property takes on the value it would have had if there were no styles in the current style origin (author, user, or user-agent). In author stylesheets (the normal case), for the purposes of the given declaration, it's as if there were no author-level styles, thus resetting the property to the default value established by the user-agent stylesheet (or by user styles, if any exist).</p>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/revert

The defined namespaces can be used to restrict the universal, type, and attribute selectors to only select elements within that namespace. The @namespace rule is generally only useful when dealing with documents containing multiple namespaces—such as HTML5 with inline SVG or MathML, or XML that mixes multiple vocabularies.</p><br><pre><code>/* Default namespace */\n@namespace url(XML-namespace-URL);\n@namespace "XML-namespace-URL";\n\n/* Prefixed namespace */\n@namespace prefix url(XML-namespace-URL);\n@namespace prefix "XML-namespace-URL";</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/@namespace

In order to appropriately style links, you need to put the :link rule before the other ones, as defined by the LVHA-order : :link — :visited — :hover — :active. It corresponds to the min-width or the min-height property, depending on the value defined for writing-mode. If the writing mode is vertically oriented, the value of min-inline-size relates to the minimal height of the element, otherwise it relates to the minimal width of the element. It relates to min-block-size, which defines the other dimension of the element.</p><br><pre><code>/* <length> values */\nmin-inline-size: 100px;\nmin-inline-size: 5em;\n\n/* <percentage> values */\nmin-inline-size: 10%;\n\n/* Keyword values */\nmin-inline-size: max-content;\nmin-inline-size: min-content;\nmin-inline-size: fit-content;\nmin-inline-size: fill-available;\n\n/* Global values */\nmin-inline-size: inherit;\nmin-inline-size: initial;\nmin-inline-size: unset;</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/min-inline-size

For example, the transform-origin of the rotate() function is the centre of rotation. (This property is applied by first translating the element by the negated value of the property, then applying the element's transform, then translating by the property value.)</p><br><pre><code>/* One-value syntax */\ntransform-origin: 2px;\ntransform-origin: bottom;\n\n/* x-offset y-offset */\ntransform-origin: 3cm 2px;\n\n/* y-offset x-offset-keyword */\ntransform-origin: 2px left;\n\n/* x-offset-keyword y-offset */\ntransform-origin: left 2px;\n\n/* x-offset-keyword y-offset-keyword */\ntransform-origin: right top;\n\n/* y-offset-keyword x-offset-keyword */\ntransform-origin: top right;\n\n/* x-offset y-offset z-offset */\ntransform-origin: 2px 30% 10px;\n\n/* y-offset x-offset-keyword z-offset */\ntransform-origin: 2px left 10px;\n\n/* x-offset-keyword y-offset z-offset */\ntransform-origin: left 5px -3px;\n\n/* x-offset-keyword y-offset-keyword z-offset */\ntransform-origin: right bottom 2cm;\n\n/* y-offset-keyword x-offset-keyword z-offset */\ntransform-origin: bottom right 2cm;\n\n/* Global values */\ntransform-origin: inherit;\ntransform-origin: initial;\ntransform-origin: unset;</code></pre>	https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/transform-origin

number	A							[Interpolation https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/number#Interpolation]\\n[Examples https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/number#Examples]\\n[Specifications https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/number#Specifications]\\n[Browser compatibility https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/CSS/number#Browser_compatibility]\\n			<p>The number CSS data type represents a number, either integer or fractional.
